FINOS Backend Audit Report (Prompt Engine)
A) Architecture assessment
Prompt engine orchestration is cleanly layered:
executor.py coordinates catalog load, dependency order, status skip logic, transaction execution, rework loop, and stop-file handling.
execution_transaction.py enforces 10-phase transactional flow: sanitize, firewall, dependency validation, repo health, precheck pytest, runner execution, guardrails, pytest, ledger update, status finalize.
prompt_runner.py provides a callback-based runner abstraction with typed PromptRunResult.
Runner interface is technically correct for current design:
Signature is Callable[[PromptDefinition], PromptRunResult].
This supports pluggable backends via closure/context capture.
CLI wiring is present:
--runner {local,none} and FINOS_PROMPT_RUNNER env resolution are implemented in cli.py.
Injection into PromptExecutionEngine(... runner_callback=...) works.
Guardrails are integrated in execution path and run after callback mutation:
Prompt sanitizer + AI firewall + repo protection + file-size checks.
Ledger updater implements append-style writes and status section management.
B) Identified bugs or design flaws
HIGH: backend/backend artifact path bug (confirmed)
local_runner.py always writes to project_root/backend/financeops/....
If CLI is run from D:\finos\backend with default --project-root ., artifact path becomes D:\finos\backend\backend\financeops\....
This is the duplicated-path issue you called out.
HIGH: Mis-scoped ledger target when project_root is backend
Default ledger path is docs/ledgers/PROMPTS_LEDGER.md relative to project_root.
Running from backend without --project-root .. writes/uses D:\finos\backend\docs\ledgers\PROMPTS_LEDGER.md instead of repo-level D:\finos\docs\ledgers\PROMPTS_LEDGER.md.
A real secondary ledger exists in repo (backend/docs/ledgers/PROMPTS_LEDGER.md), proving this drift happened.
MEDIUM: No guard against ambiguous CLI working-directory usage
CLI does not auto-normalize to repo root, so same command behaves differently by cwd.
MEDIUM: Runner-reported file list is not authoritative for guardrails
Guardrails validate repository snapshot diff, not run_result.modified_files.
This is mostly safe, but ledger can record paths that were never validated by file-size check if callback reports custom list.
LOW: Ledger parsing/writing is markdown-string based, not schema-validated
latest_status_map does naive pipe splitting; escaped content and malformed rows can reduce parsing integrity.
C) Security risks
Prompt sanitization/firewall is substring-based and easy to evade via obfuscation/encoding once a powerful runner is introduced.
No sandbox boundary exists for future runners; callback can execute arbitrary local code.
Append-only policy for ledger is enforcement-at-runtime only; no tamper-evident chain/hash for ledger rows.
Current local runner stores prompt preview in artifact files; sensitive prompt text can leak into filesystem artifacts.
D) Scalability limitations
Full repository snapshot twice per prompt (before/after) scales poorly on large repos.
pytest -q baseline precheck is executed per prompt, and pytest runs again post-execution per prompt.
Rework loop can multiply pytest/snapshot cost by attempts.
Ledger is flat markdown append; lookup and reconciliation are O(file size) string scans.
E) Recommended improvements
Fix root resolution contract:
Resolve an explicit repo root once in CLI and pass normalized root to engine/runner.
Reject ambiguous project_root when catalog/ledger resolve outside root unless explicitly allowed.
Harden local runner pathing:
Build artifact dir from canonical module location or configurable relative root, not hardcoded backend/... prefix.
Add CLI/path integration tests:
Run from D:\finos\backend and assert artifacts/ledger go to repo root with intended command.
Add env override tests:
FINOS_PROMPT_RUNNER=local, invalid env value behavior, and precedence vs --runner.
Add stronger security policy before CodexRunner:
Structured allowlist for file targets.
Optional subprocess/network isolation.
Stronger prompt policy checks (token/AST or policy engine).
Add ledger integrity controls:
Optional hash chain per row and strict schema validation for status section rows.
F) Code quality issues
Path semantics are implicit and fragile across cwd.
Ledger format handling is permissive and can accumulate mixed table styles.
Some behavior-critical assumptions are only tested with tmp_path roots, not real repository layout.
Error handling in runner mode resolution is good, but ergonomics/documentation for correct project_root usage are weak.
G) Readiness for CodexRunner implementation
Status: Conditionally ready, not production-ready yet.
Ready aspects:
Runner interface abstraction exists.
Execution pipeline and guardrails are already integrated.
CLI injection path exists.
Blocking gaps before CodexRunner:
Path-root ambiguity (backend/backend and split-ledger risk).
Security model too weak for a powerful code-writing runner.
Missing end-to-end tests for real cwd/project-root combinations and env-based runner selection.

2. The 3 Real Issues We Must Fix
Codex found many things, but only three are truly important now.

Issue 1 — Path Bug (backend/backend)
Artifacts landed here:

D:\finos\backend\backend\financeops\...
because the runner assumes:

project_root/backend/...
but you launched the CLI from:

D:\finos\backend
So the fix is simple.

Artifact path should be:

project_root / financeops / prompt_engine / _runner_artifacts
NOT:

project_root / backend / financeops / ...
This removes the duplicate folder.

Issue 2 — Ledger Drift Risk
You currently have two possible ledgers:

D:\finos\docs\ledgers\PROMPTS_LEDGER.md
D:\finos\backend\docs\ledgers\PROMPTS_LEDGER.md
Which one gets written depends on where you run the CLI.

That is dangerous.

The CLI should always resolve the repo root automatically.

Correct behaviour:

repo_root
 ├ backend
 ├ docs
 ├ infra
and the engine must always use:

repo_root/docs/ledgers/PROMPTS_LEDGER.md
Issue 3 — Security before CodexRunner
Right now the runner could theoretically modify any file.

Before introducing CodexRunner we must restrict modifications to:

backend/
docs/
tests/
and block changes to:

infra/
docker/
.env
.git
This is a simple allowlist guardrail.

3. What We Should NOT Do Yet
Do NOT introduce CodexRunner yet.

The audit is correct:

"Conditionally ready, not production ready"

We first fix the root resolution issue.

4. Correct CLI Command Going Forward
Until we patch the CLI, run commands like this:

cd D:\finos\backend
Then:

python -m financeops.prompt_engine.cli run `
--project-root .. `
--catalog docs/prompts/PROMPTS_CATALOG.md `
--ledger docs/ledgers/PROMPTS_LEDGER.md `
--runner local
This forces the correct root.

main problem is when we run this, codex is executive from every codex window in vscode, may be should fix this

Yes — this is a real problem, and you identified the correct root cause.

When Codex runs inside VS Code, every window with the extension active can start its own agent session. That means multiple windows can try to execute the same task or read/write the same repository at the same time. 

So what you’re seeing is:

VSCode Window 1  → Codex agent
VSCode Window 2  → Codex agent
VSCode Window 3  → Codex agent
All of them attempt to execute prompts.

Your prompt engine then gets parallel executions, which causes chaos.

Why this happens
VS Code allows multiple agent sessions in parallel, each operating independently. 

Each window:

has its own extension process

has its own Codex agent

can run commands

can modify files

So if you have:

3 VSCode windows
you effectively have:

3 Codex executors
running on the same repo.

That is very dangerous for your architecture.

What your architecture actually needs
Your system must enforce one execution authority.

Think of it like a database lock.

Only one runner should be able to execute prompts.

Prompt Engine
      ↓
Execution Lock
      ↓
Runner (Codex)
If another window tries to run → blocked.

The correct solution (simple and robust)
Add an execution lock file.

Example:

.repo/finos_prompt_engine.lock
Execution flow:

Start prompt
     ↓
Check lock
     ↓
If locked → exit
If free → acquire lock
     ↓
Run prompt
     ↓
Release lock
Example implementation idea
Before prompt execution:

lock_file = repo_root / ".finos_prompt_engine.lock"

if lock_file.exists():
    raise RuntimeError("Prompt engine already running")

lock_file.write_text(str(os.getpid()))
After execution:

lock_file.unlink()
Even better solution (enterprise-grade)
Use file lock instead of file existence.

Example:

portalocker
filelock
This prevents stale locks.

Example:

from filelock import FileLock

lock = FileLock(".finos_prompt_engine.lock")

with lock:
    run_prompt()
Now only one process in the entire machine can run the prompt engine.

Even better (future improvement)
Later you can introduce a Prompt Supervisor process.

VSCode Window
       ↓
Codex
       ↓
Prompt Supervisor
       ↓
Prompt Engine
Only the supervisor runs prompts.

This completely prevents multi-window issues.

My recommendation
Implement this immediately before CodeRunner:

Add a global execution lock
backend/.prompt_engine.lock
Then enforce it in:

executor.py
before execution begins.

Result
Your architecture becomes safe:

Multiple VSCode windows
        ↓
Prompt Engine Lock
        ↓
Single Runner
        ↓
Code changes
No parallel Codex execution.

One more thing (very important)
When you introduce CodeRunner, this lock becomes mandatory.

Without it, two Codex agents could:

Agent A → rewrite file
Agent B → rewrite same file
Repo corruption.

If you want, I can also show you a much stronger architecture used by large AI-coding systems that prevents this problem entirely without relying only on file locks.


ask codex to fix this

Yes — you should ask Codex to fix it by enforcing a single execution lock so only one Codex runner can execute at a time, regardless of how many VS Code windows are open.

Your problem is exactly a multi-process race condition. Multiple VS Code windows start separate Python processes, and they all try to run the prompt engine simultaneously. When multiple processes access the same resources without synchronization, corruption or conflicts can occur. Using a file lock is the standard solution to prevent concurrent execution. 

So the fix is straightforward: introduce a global execution lock in the prompt engine.

Prompt to give Codex
Give Codex this exact task:

Implement a global execution lock for the FINOS prompt engine to prevent
multiple Codex runners from executing simultaneously across multiple
VSCode windows or processes.

Problem:
When multiple VSCode windows are open, Codex may run the prompt engine
from several processes at the same time, causing concurrent execution.

Solution:
Introduce a process-wide execution lock using a file lock.

Implementation requirements:

1. Add dependency
Use the filelock library.

2. Create lock location
<repo_root>/.finos_prompt_engine.lock

3. Modify executor entry point

File:
backend/financeops/prompt_engine/executor.py

Before starting prompt execution:

Acquire the lock.

Example pattern:

from filelock import FileLock, Timeout

lock_path = repo_root / ".finos_prompt_engine.lock"
lock = FileLock(lock_path)

with lock:
    run_prompt_execution()

If another process already holds the lock:
- log a message
- exit gracefully

4. Lock scope

The lock must protect the entire execution pipeline:

Prompt loading
Dependency resolution
Runner execution
Guardrails
pytest execution
Ledger update

5. Failure safety

The lock must automatically release if the process crashes.

6. Logging

If lock acquisition fails:

log:
"Prompt engine execution blocked: another runner is active"

7. Tests

Add test:

backend/tests/prompt_engine/test_execution_lock.py

Test cases:

- second execution blocked
- lock released after run
- lock released after exception

8. Do not change existing architecture.

The lock should only wrap execution entry points.
What will happen after this fix
Your system will behave like this:

VSCode Window A
        │
VSCode Window B
        │
VSCode Window C
        │
        ▼
Execution Lock
        │
Only ONE runner allowed
        │
Prompt Engine
        │
Runner
Every other process will immediately exit.

Why this is the correct fix
Without this lock:

Runner A → modifies repo
Runner B → modifies repo
Runner C → modifies repo
Result:

git corruption
test failures
ledger conflicts
With the lock:

Runner A executes
Runner B waits or exits
Runner C waits or exits
Safe.

One more improvement (later)
Eventually you should run the prompt engine outside VSCode entirely, for example:

terminal
CI worker
supervisor process
VSCode should only trigger it, not run it directly.

But for now, the execution lock is the correct immediate fix.

If you want, I can also show you a much stronger architecture used by autonomous coding systems (OpenAI / Anthropic style) that eliminates this VSCode multi-window problem completely.

Executor now removes stale .finos_prompt_engine.lock only if it can safely acquire that lock non-blocking first.

That means:

active runner → lock preserved
stale lock → auto removed
This prevents the multi-VSCode runner issue you were worried about.

This is essentially:

AI-driven CI pipeline.
